<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hey_Jude&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="reflist columns references-column-count references-column-count-2" style="-moz-column-count: 2; -webkit-column-count: 2; column-count: 2; list-style-type: decimal;">
<ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-13"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-13">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Griffith added that he and his fellow Iveys were "gobsmacked" by the performance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECross2005367_12-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECross2005367-12">[12]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-24"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-24">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In a 1971 interview with Jonathan Cott, Lennon recalled his and McCartney's conversation: "Ah, it's me! I said, it's <i>me</i>! He says, no it's <i>me</i>. I said, check, we're going through the same bit."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESchaffner1978108_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchaffner1978108-23">[22]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-39"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-39">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Produced by the National Music Council of Great Britain,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELeng200635_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELeng200635-38">[36]</a></sup> the documentary was released in October 1969.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEverett1999194_36-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEverett1999194-36">[34]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-49"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-49">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Described by <a href="/wiki/Ian_MacDonald" title="Ian MacDonald">Ian MacDonald</a> as "a tense moment",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMacDonald1998267fn_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMacDonald1998267fn-46">[43]</a></sup> this disagreement between Harrison and McCartney was recalled by the pair in a similar argument they had while filming <i><a href="/wiki/Let_It_Be_(1970_film)" title="Let It Be (1970 film)">Let It Be</a></i> in January 1969,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEverett1999194_36-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEverett1999194-36">[34]</a></sup> regarding the lead guitar part on "<a href="/wiki/Two_of_Us_(song)" title="Two of Us (song)">Two of Us</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESounes2010237_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESounes2010237-47">[44]</a></sup> Partly as a result of McCartney's criticism, Harrison briefly quit the band on 10 January.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEverett1999194_36-3"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEverett1999194-36">[34]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMiles2001328_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMiles2001328-48">[45]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-59"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-59">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In 2013 McCartney agreed to write the foreword to Sheffield's book "Life on Two Legs", partly because of his positive experience when recording "Hey Jude".</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-68"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-68">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Writing in his 2006 memoir, Emerick says that "Obviously something at Trident had been misaligned", and the solution for "Hey Jude" was to add "massive amounts of treble <a href="/wiki/Equalization_(audio)" title="Equalization (audio)">equalization</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEmerickMassey2006260_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEmerickMassey2006260-67">[62]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-78"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-78">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Toft adds: "because it had been bounced down [mixed] with the main vocal, it could not be removed. I just managed to bring the fader down for a split second on the mix to try to lessen the effect."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERyanKehew2006288.E2.80.9389_77-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERyanKehew2006288.E2.80.9389-77">[71]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-93"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-93">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The catalogue numbers for "Hey Jude"/"Revolution" – Apple 5722 in the UK and 2276 in the US – were consistent with the numerical sequencing of the Beatles' previous releases on Parlophone and Capitol. Apple's other three debut singles followed a new sequencing, starting with "Those Were the Days", which was issued as Apple 2 and Apple 1801.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECastlemanPodrazik1976301_92-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECastlemanPodrazik1976301-92">[85]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-112"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-112">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Having told Smith, "The truth about me is that I'm pleasantly insincere", McCartney said: "You can't pretend to me that an <a href="/wiki/Oxfam" title="Oxfam">Oxfam</a> ad can reach down into the depths of your soul and actually make you feel for those [starving] people – more, for instance, than you feel about getting a new car."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMiles2001306_87-4"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMiles2001306-87">[80]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-151"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-151">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">EMI archives do not record the names of the studio musicians, but it has been established that two of the cellists were <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Kok" title="Alexander Kok">Alexander "Bobby" Kok</a> and Peter Halling, and two of the flautists were Bill Jackman and Brian Warren.</span></li>
</ol>
</div>
